1 Introduction
1.1 Background
The Downer Concept of Operations (ConOps) for the Ormeau Facility was originally included in
Part A of Schedule C3, Contractor’s Proposal (Ormeau Facility), 5.2.2 Ormeau Facility Site Layout
Proposal. Supported by the Operational Rail Modelling, this section of the Proposal sought to
demonstrate how train movements to and from the Facility and its constituent parts would be
managed to achieve the requirements of the Performance Specification, Schedule C1.
This document has been progressively updated to reflect the developing design of the Ormeau
Facility and now incorporates detailed design inputs and cross references to the State’s document
“Ormeau Concept of Operations - Sector 1 South (M2VL) ETCS Upgrade Project” (TMR ConOps)
with document reference “3215406-TMR-1016RAOM-RPT-000001 (revision 3 at the time of
writing).
The TMR ConOps document informs ongoing discussions with interfacing projects, notably the
mainline connection with the Logan and Gold Coast Faster Rail (LGCFR) project and the rollout of
European Train Control Level 2 (ETCS). The TMR ConOps is primarily concerned with operations
by Queensland Rail’s Rail Traffic Crew between the Gold Coast mainline, Ormeau Stabling Yard
and the Maintenance Facility Handover/Handback points.
Following the State’s direction to expand the extent of ETCS into the Ormeau Stabling Yard, the
TMR ConOps now defines the concept of operations of the Ormeau Stabling signalling system. For
this reason, details of the Ormeau Stabling ETCS signalling operations have been removed from
the Downer ConOps and replaced with cross referencing to the TMR ConOps.
Signalling technical details for both the ETCS system in the Ormeau Stabling Yard and the
conventional Remote Controlled Signalling (RCS) system in the Maintenance Facility have been
replaced in this revision of the Downer ConOps with cross referencing to the following documents:
 Ormeau Stabling Yard ETCS signalling by State:
o Ormeau Stabling Yard - Signalling Arrangement AS925.1_1A_003
 Sequence Alliance reference 3215406-SEQ-1016SGET-MSD-AS0001_1.0
 Hitachi reference B2V-SIG-WYS-D09-024.001_00.00_1
o ETCS Stabling Operations - AU1300704_NT20250314_1.1
 Ormeau Maintenance Facility RCS Signalling by Downer:
o User Requirements Specification – QTMP Ormeau Depot
 QTMP-MNT-DOW-PM-SPC-000001_4
o Signalling Technical Requirements Specification – QTMP Ormeau Depot
 QTMP-MNT-DOW-PM-SPC-000002_4
o Ormeau Maintenance Facility Signalling Arrangement Plan AS924_1A-015
 Downer reference QTMP-DOW-OMFRNSI00-DRG-AS0001_E

2 Review & Consultation
This Downer ConOps has been progressively updated as the Ormeau Facility design has
developed. As part of the Detailed Design Review (DDR) process for the Ormeau Facility,
feedback from State and Queensland Rail (QR) was discussed and agreed and incorporated with
minor updates to the previous Baseline Layout. The changes are summarised as follows:
1. Tracks were renamed and renumbered according to Queensland Rail Operational
preferences
2. The catch point on the North Entrance Road was moved further south, away from the
bridge over Halfway Creek to a position immediately north of the Wash Road turnout
3. The positions of the Maintenance Facility train gates were confirmed with shunt necks
being external to Maintenance Facility train gates – it was not feasible to place the gates
outside the shunt necks due to insufficient space at both ends of the site
4. Maintenance Facility zone of Rail Infrastructure Manager (RIM) was confirmed (refer Figure
1) as being within the Maintenance Facility train gates plus the North Shunt and South
Shunt, with RIM boundaries being at:
a. North – on the North Maintenance Road between the turnout to North Shunt and
turnout to Link Road
b. South - on the South Maintenance Road between the turnout to South Shunt and
turnout from South Entrance Road
5. Turnout configurations were optimised within both the Stabling and Maintenance yards
This Downer Concept of Operations (Rev D) retains the operating principles for the Ormeau
Facility, ensuring that the Maintenance Facility is:
 Functionally separate from the Stabling Yard and Queensland Rail’s RIM zone
 Managed by Downer’s Yard Master within their own, separate control system with all train
movements undertaken without interaction with Queensland Rail Operations, apart from
entry/ exist to/ from the Maintenance Facility
2.1 Layout Baseline
The DDR arrangement which incorporates the changes discussed above is shown in Figure 1. This
arrangement accommodates 6-car and 9-car holding as shown in Figure 2.

3 Site Operations – Areas of
Control
The Ormeau Maintenance Facility and Stabling Yard will incorporate the requirements of the
nominated Rail Infrastructure Manager (RIM) and Rollingstock Operator (RSO) for each location.
The Queensland Rail controlled Stabling Yard and the Downer controlled Maintenance Facility will
contain clearly defined areas of control and interface points at the Control Boundary Boards on the
North Maintenance Road and South Maintenance Roads – refer Figure 1 for indicative position of
RIM boundaries which are coincident with Control Boundary Boards. For more detailed
information, refer to documents as listed in section 1.1:
 State’s Stabling Yard AS Plan and ETCS Stabling Operations
 Downer’s Maintenance Facility AS Plan and User Requirement Specification (URS) and
Signalling Technical Requirements Specification (TRS)
This Downer ConOps document allows Downer to complete all required Multiple Unit movements
within its area of control, without impeding Queensland Rail-controlled sections. Further, this will
enable the completion of all maintenance activities without interruption to the Mainline or Stabling
Figure 1 in the previous section demonstrates the following key areas of control:
 Track centreline colours represent the signalling control areas.
 Gold lines are controlled by Queensland Rail - Rail Management Centre (RMC)
 Blue lines are controlled by the Downer’s Yardmaster.
The following roads will be controlled by Queensland Rail’s RMC:
 North Entrance Road, Middle Road and Wash Road
 North Maintenance Road up to and including Link Road
 All Stabling Roads
 South Maintenance Road between South Entrance Road and South Shunt
 South Entrance Road
The following roads will be controlled by Downer’s Yardmaster:
 North Maintenance Road up to and including the North Shunt
 All Maintenance Facility Roads
 South Maintenance Road up to and including the South Shunt
The following areas will require a signalling slot request:
 For moves out of the Maintenance Facility via either the North Maintenance Road or the
South Maintenance Road, Downer’s Yardmaster is required to request the slot from RMC
 For moves into the Maintenance Facility via the North Maintenance Road or the South
Maintenance Road, RMC is required to request the slot from Downer’s Yardmaster
Ideally, catch points at each end of the Maintenance Facility would be included to provide roll-out
protection to the Queensland Rail controlled area, however due to geometric constraints, this is not
feasible. As an alternative, turnouts to both the North Shunt and South Shunt have been
normalised in the divergent direction into the shunt necks, providing a similar level of protection.
.
Downer EDI Limited
ABN 97 003 872 848 www.downergroup.com

QTMP-MNT-DOW-SM-RPT-000012 rev D
3.1 Maintenance Facility
Areas inside Maintenance Facility Train Gates, including the North and South Shunt necks are
considered a yard environment and an operational speed of 8km/h applies.
All roads in the Maintenance Facility will be conventionally signalled with Remote Controlled
Signalling (RCS) – for details refer to the Maintenance Facility URS, TRS, and AS Plan as
referenced in section 1.1. All points will be powered with available routes from the Maintenance
Facility train gate to all roads within the Maintenance Facility including the shunt necks. Handover
points will be available on all roads in the Maintenance Facility except Road 5 - south.
The RCS signalling data will be configured with and input into a Depot Personnel Protection
System (DPPS) to allow route setting into and out of the Maintenance Facility building and around
the yard including the Wheel Lathe building, Presentation Platform and Bio/Graffiti Wash building.
Personnel in the Maintenance Facility building will be protected at the north and south ends by
derailers which retract when a route is set into the Maintenance Facility building. The DPPS
including derailers will be managed by Downer under Downer’s RIM accreditation.
3.2 Queensland Rail Stabling
Control of all roads outside the Maintenance Facility train gates (with the exception of the North
and South Shunts) will be under an ETCS system and all points will be powered with routes
available from the North and South Entrance Roads into all roads within the Queensland Rail
Ormeau Stabling Yard. Routes will also be available from all roads to and from the Middle Road,
Wash Road and Link Road.
3.3 Mainline Connections & ETCS Transition Points.
Control of the mainline and the Ormeau Stabling Yard will be under the ETCS Level 2 system.
State’s Ormeau Facility signalling arrangement plan AS925.1-1A-003 shows signalling control
interface boundaries in the following areas:
 North Maintenance Road between turnouts on Link Road and North Shunt
 South Maintenance Road between turnouts on South Entrance Road and South Shunt
The Maintenance Facility RCS signalling arrangement plan has been developed in conjunction with
the State’s ETCS design and shows the positioning of Control Boundary Boards in similar locations
to that shown on the ETCS AS Plan.
According to the TMR ConOps, the Maintenance Facility will be configured in the ETCS system as
a Permanent Shunting Area. As such, trains entering/ departing the Maintenance Facility are
required to transition to/ from an ETCS Shunt Mode respectively.
This is done through the transition zone which extends on each side of the Control Boundary and
is configured to safely and efficiently transfer control between Queensland Rail RMC and the
Downer Yardmaster. For details of the transition through different ETCS Modes in this zone, refer
to the TMR ConOps (section 3.4.4 Transitions at the time of writing).
Refer to Figure 3 for a diagram of signalling transition points and areas of signalling control .
Downer EDI Limited
ABN 97 003 872 848 www.downergroup.com

3.4 Site Movements Overview
QTMP Multiple Units will typically arrive and depart the Ormeau Facility via the northern end by
utilising the North Entrance Road, Middle Road and the Wash Road. The Link Road effectively
provides a fourth option for Stabling access if required. The Ormeau Facility is also accessible for
arriving and departing trains from the south via the South Entrance Road. QTMP Multiple Units
upon arriving to the site via either direction are able to be directed to the Stabling Yard, the Wash
Road or directly to the Maintenance Facility for maintenance activities.
In terms of accessing the Train Wash, if Stabling is full and/or the direct path to the Wash Road is
blocked by another train on the same Stabling road, then operational flexibility is reduced. It is
preferable, however, for trains to be washed on the way in from the north as indicated in the TMR
ConOps (section 4.6.1.2 Arrival to Stabling Roads via Train Wash/AVIS Road).
It is anticipated that movements from Stabling to the Train Wash and back and also for trains
arriving from the South for instance, will be planned such that marshalling access to the Train
Wash from Stabling is available and not impeded by trains already stabled at the northern end.
In terms of arrival road impacts, again, marshalling to the Train Wash at peak times is not
preferred, however, it is unlikely that the headways (mainline to Stabling) will be adversely affected
by a single marshalling move from Stabling to the Train Wash. Washing on the way out is also an
option for trains stabled at the Southern end of the yard or trains entering from the south.
It is acknowledged that State’s timetabling and service planning is ongoing and more frequent
entry and exit moves from the south may be required beyond the occasional moves originally
envisaged. Details will be worked through in the development of State’s ETCS URS/TRS and
Requirements AS Plan, once timetabling and associated train planning has been completed by
Queensland Rail.
During normal operations, QTMP Multiple Units will be marshalled daily between the Maintenance
Facility and the Stabling Yard for maintenance or presentation requirements. These marshalling
Downer EDI Limited
ABN 97 003 872 848 www.downergroup.com
--- PAGE 12 ---
QTMP-MNT-DOW-SM-RPT-000012 rev D
movements are able to be completed via either the Link Road or the South Entrance Road to
minimise any impacts on Mainline entries and departures.
Downer’s Automatic Vehicle Inspection System (AVIS) is located on the Train Wash road to collect
data on each train every 7seven days.
3.5 Downer and Queensland Rail Interface
The interface between each of the sections will be managed by the signalling systems and the
signalling slot process. Movements between the Maintenance Facility and Stabling will be
completed by the Rail Traffic Crew. The route set will be established and managed by either
Queensland Rail RMC, or the Downer Yardmaster.
3.6 Handover and Handback Locations
The Maintenance Facility’s designated handover points will be established to support the smooth,
safe, and effective arrival and departure of Multiple Units. These locations will have safe access
platforms for Rail Traffic Crew to enter and disembark the QTMP Multiple Units with safe,
compliant pedestrian pathways for access and egress to the Handover/Handback locations.
Compliance will be demonstrated through the relevant detailed design packages.
Designated Handover and Handback locations will be provided in the Stabling Yard and on the
Northern and Southern side of the Maintenance Facility building where most of the entry and exit
movements will be completed. These will be located on each Maintenance Road external to the
Train Maintenance Building, and preceding specialist equipment. This will allow for the direct
delivery of Multiple Units to a specific Maintenance Road, where the required infrastructure or
specialist equipment is located. Further, it will segregate the movement to any existing activities
that are in the process of being completed.
Consideration has been given to the Rail Traffic Crew’s walking distance and this has been
designed to be as efficient as possible. Analysis completed and submitted with the Contractor's
Proposal shows that the proposed Rail Traffic Crew Building location results in walking distances
that are comparable to existing stabling yards and under all scenarios are less than 800 metres
and 15 minutes. Current Calculated walking distances and times are summarised as follows:
Destination: Distance (m): Walking Time (min):
Furthest stabling location 521m 9:46
Northern handover 313m 5:52
Presentation Platform 353m 6:37
Southern handover 508m 9:32
The handover/handback procedure is defined in detail within the Downer document QTMP-DHC-
DOW-PM-PLN-000035 Handover & Handback Plan.
3.7 Stabling Yard
The Stabling Yard will comprise 10 stabling roads with capacity to stable two Multiple Units per
road at a total of 20 x 6 car sets. Each road will be provided with a pedestrian pathway with lighting
and train access platforms.
Downer EDI Limited
ABN 97 003 872 848 www.downergroup.com
--- PAGE 13 ---
QTMP-MNT-DOW-SM-RPT-000012 rev D
Handover points will be available in two locations on each Stabling Road with personnel access via
the cab provided by train access platforms at both ends of each Stabling location (i.e., four train
access platforms per road.
On each road, 10m long train access platforms will be provided at the south end of the northern
position and at the north end of the southern position to accommodate future robotic cleaning
equipment, subject to QR acceptance of a safety risk assessment.
The Stabling Yard will also contain an unwired road for track machines configured in accordance
with the Performance Specification for the Ormeau Facility.
Areas inside Ormeau Stabling Yard Train Gates are considered a yard environment and a speed of
8km/h applies.
Areas outside Train Gates are to have speeds limits applied and documented in the State’s ETCS
AS Plan to:
 support safe operations
 support operational requirements on the Wash Road
 achieve of arrival and departure performance
Refer section 4.2 of Appendix 2 of this Downer ConOps for more detail of cleaning activities in the
Stabling Yard.
3.7.1 Train Wash and AVIS
Below is an overview of movements on the Train Wash Road – for more detail, refer to TMR
ConOps (section 4.6.1.2 Arrival to Stabling Roads via Train Wash/AVIS Road). Details of the
operation of the Train Wash and the nature of its interface with Queensland Rail Operations are
under development and will be documented in the TMR ConOps document.
The automatic exterior train wash will be utilised by QTMP and NGR fleet types and managed by
Queensland Rail. The AVIS is for use with QTMP trains only and will be managed by Downer -
non-QTMP units may pass through the AVIS, however data will not be available.
By having these facilities adjacent to the entry of the Stabling Yard, it will allow the Multiple Units to
be subjected to frequent inspections and cleans prior to the units entering the Stabling Yard. Whilst
both Train Wash and AVIS are bi-directional, it is anticipated trains will be predominantly routed
along the Train Wash / AVIS road following arrival from the Northern Connection.
The train wash is capable of washing 10 multiple units per hour in side-wash mode, or 3 multiple
units per hour in full-wash mode. Queensland Rail will be responsible for the scheduling of each
train to undergo an external wash plant clean on a regular basis.
Once a train has arrived outside the Train Wash and the Train Wash is activated, Rail Traffic Crew
will proceed in accordance with the Train Wash coloured-light indicators (linked to the required
wash cycle type) displayed within the Train Wash building and approximately 120m either side of
the building.
Refer Table 13 of Appendix 2 of this Downer ConOps for a list of AVIS functionality.
QTMP trains are currently assumed to go through the AVIS every 7 days (averaging 10 trains per
day). The AVIS will detect QTMP trains and automatically take measurements for QTMP only.
Before entry into AVIS, Movement Authority is required through to a point such that the train will
not be required to stop or alter speed within the AVIS building. If a train is forced to stop before
clearing the equipment or the speed deviates by 10% of the entrance speed, then the collection of
maintenance data will be void.
Downer EDI Limited
ABN 97 003 872 848 www.downergroup.com
--- PAGE 14 ---
QTMP-MNT-DOW-SM-RPT-000012 rev D
Therefore, a route must be set by the RMC and a Movement Authority provided through to the
allocated Stabling Road, allowing the train to proceed through the Train Gates and into the
Stabling Roads.
Maximum operational speeds on the Train Wash Road are as follows:
 Through Train Wash building:
o Full-wash or side-wash modes: 3km/h
o No-wash mode: 8km/h
 Through AVIS:
o Constant speed of 3-8km/h maintaining speed through entire length of train.

3.9 Roles and Responsibilities
Each area of the Ormeau Facility will have roles to co-ordinate and manage safe movements
within their own area of control, and co-ordinated movements between the Maintenance Facility,
the Stabling Yard and Mainline via the agreed interface.
3.9.1 Downer
The key role supporting the movement of trains within the Maintenance Facility will be the Downer
Yardmaster. This will be supported by Downer's Technicians who will be trained and competent to
drive trains in the Maintenance Facility. Downer's roles and responsibilities are captured in Table 2.
Table 2: Downer Roles and Responsibilities
Role Responsibilities
Downer’s  Path setting, approval, and control of all Multiple Unit movements within the
Yardmaster Maintenance Facility
 Acceptance of Multiple Units into the Maintenance Facility from the Mainline to
designated Handover/Handback locations
 Acceptance of Multiple Units into the Maintenance Facility from the Stabling Yard
 Release of Multiple Units from the Maintenance Facility to the Stabling Yard
 Release of Multiple Units from the Maintenance Facility designated
Handover/Handback locations to the Mainline.
Technician  Trained and competent staff authorised to drive Multiple Units within the
Maintenance Facility under the direction of the Downer Yardmaster.

Table 3: Queensland Rail’s Roles and Responsibilities
Role Responsibilities

 Path setting, approval, and control of all Multiple Unit movements between the

Crew infrastructure.

Rail infrastructure and the Maintenance Facility via the agreed interface protocols.
3.10 Site Communications
For communications between Rail Traffic Crew and the Downer Yardmaster, the Queensland Rail
train radio depot operations channel will be used. Each Queensland Rail train will be fitted with a
train radio console that is used by the Rail Traffic Crew to communicate with the RMC and a
portable handheld radio to communicate with depots on the depot operations channel. This means
that either radio can perform the other task if a failure occurs.
For communications between Rail Traffic Crew and RMC, the train radio will be used (for example,
when departing the Maintenance Facility).
For communications between the Downer Yardmaster and RMC, a dedicated Enhanced Radio
System (ERS) will be used by the Yardmaster either via a desktop ERS radio located in the
Operations Office inside the Maintenance Facility building or by a dedicated ERS hand-held radio.
3.11 Training and Competency
Trained, competent, and authorised Downer maintenance Technicians will complete Multiple Unit
set movements within the Maintenance Facility under the control of the Downer Yardmaster.
Downer will train maintenance Technicians to operate the trains at the Maintenance Facility in
accordance with the standard mandated by Rail Safety National Law (RSNL). A Competency
Management System (CMS) will ensure that driving standards are adhered to during operations.
3.12 Maintenance Facility Systems
The operation of the Maintenance Facility will incorporate multiple systems that interface between
different personnel within Downer and Queensland Rail to effectively control Multiple Unit
movements between each site and the Mainline. Table 4 identifies and details systems for use at
Ormeau Maintenance Facility.

 All the points will be powered and interlocked with the signals

Depot Personnel The DPPS will provide the following:
Protection System  An interface with the signalling to control the derailers installed either side of
the Maintenance Facility
 Control shunt signals inside and outside the shed to control departure and
arrival of trains inside the Maintenance Facility building
 Interlock with the OHLE for detection of isolation and the cranes to ensure
they are parked before movements commence, with the high-level access to
ensure all gates are secured. Sensors are in place to ensure there are no
obstructions to the road by plant or mobile platforms and will ensure that all
personnel have ceased working on the train prior to movement commencing.

and communicates set positions on-site at the Maintenance Facility and
includes the following features and benefits:
 It is populated in ‘real time’ by the Downer Yardmaster as set movements
are planned and executed, and is visible on computers, tablets, and smart
phones
 It is a primary visualisation tool for the Maintenance Delivery Manager to
ascertain the exact location and status of trains on the Maintenance Facility.

In terms of Train Wash capacity, conceptually, it will be required to wash one train every 480s (8
minutes), approximately, if every second train entering the Facility is sent via the Train Wash. The
wash plant has a specified capacity of 10MUs an hour for straight through washing or one train
every 6 minutes, which is above the peak operational need.
Further details relevant to the operation of the train wash road will be developed and included in
State’s ETCS signalling URS/TRS/Requirements AS Plan.

4 Movements between Facility
and Mainline
Movements to and from the Mainline to the Ormeau Facility will be achieved from the north and
from the south. The primary route in and out will be from the north.
The Performance Specification for the Ormeau Facility defines the operational requirements for the
Facility and, specifically, the need for trains to enter and exit the Mainline via a northern entry such
that they do not impart movement or speed restrictions on following or preceding trains on the
Mainline, operating at a technical headway of 120 seconds.
This requirement is illustrated in Figure 5 below with target technical headways for basic entry and
exit movements.
Figure 5: Basic Operational Requirement for entry and exit to the Facility
Following the State’s direction to expand the extent of ETCS into the Ormeau Stabling Yard, the
TMR ConOps now describes in detail the movements between the Ormeau Facility and the
mainline. The Downer ConOps no longer includes rail operational modelling information as
required by Schedule C1 Performance Specification (Ormeau Facility) as the responsibility for this
has been transferred to State as part of the ETCS scope change. For information, the performance
criteria are listed below in Table 6.
Table 6: Operational Performance Requirements
Criteria Schedule C1 clause 3.2.2 The Ormeau Facility must integrate with
the TMR signalling design for the Logan to Gold Coast Faster Rail
Project proven using operational simulation modelling in RailSys to:
3.2.2.b.i receiving two consecutive Train Consists travelling at the Technical
Headway of 120 seconds exiting the Up Mainline in the up
direction, without impeding a following train travelling on the Up
Mainline at Technical Headway of 120 seconds;
3.2.2.b.ii receiving a Train Consist exiting the Up Mainline in the up direction,
without impeding a following train travelling at Technical Headway
of 120 seconds.

--- PAGE 20 ---
QTMP-MNT-DOW-SM-RPT-000012 rev D
3.2.2.b.iii despatching a Train Consist crossing the Up Mainline in the down direction
between two trains travelling at Technical Headway of 240 seconds, without
impeding the approaching train on the Up Mainline, to stop between the Up
and Down Mainlines;
3.2.2.b.iv despatching a Train Consist from stop between the Up Mainline and Down
Mainlines to the Down Mainline in the down direction, between two trains
travelling at 240 second headway, without impeding the following train on the
Down Mainline; and
3.2.2.b.v despatching a Train Consist from stop between the Up Mainline and Down
Mainline, in the down direction to the Down Mainline and being within a 120
second Technical Headway from the preceding Mainline Train Consist.
Despatching trains from stabling requires a crossing of the Up Mainline, and
a merge to the Down Mainline. This movement is to be assumed to be
undertaken in 2 separate movements on the basis that timetabled train paths
on the Up Mainline and Down Mainline are not synchronised.
Notwithstanding the specific requirements of Schedule C1, the facility will predominantly support
services starting and terminating at Beenleigh, without impacting through services to/from the Gold
Coast. State has confirmed that alternate services on the mainline will start or terminate at
Beenleigh with the remainder starting or terminating at the Gold Coast, combined, these will make
up a 120s headway (technical) mainline service. This being the case, the Facility needs to launch
or retrieve services between the mainline and stabling every 240s, i.e. the Beenleigh trains, not
every train on the mainline. Initial static modelling has demonstrated that the Facility will
accommodate successive entry and exit moves between the stabling yard and the mainline at 240
second headways.
The track infrastructure for the Northern Mainline connection has been configured to allow the
entry and exit speeds necessary to meet the Operational Requirements based on 1 in 16 turnouts.
Entry and exit moves will be under the control of the Queensland Rail RMC and will allow for
arriving trains to exit the Mainline without disrupting the Mainline headway of 120 seconds as
discussed above. Operational modelling by State will incorporate the ETCS signalling principles to
verify the technical headways are achieved.
The layout of the Facility allows trains to access the Maintenance Facility from Stabling and from
the Mainline at both ends of the Facility. It is envisaged that train movements between
Maintenance Facility and Mainline will occur in off-peak periods when there is less pressure on
maintaining headway. There is sufficient track capacity to hold trains clear of the Mainline and
arrival/departure roads for these Mainline/Maintenance Facility movements to occur.
As discussed previously, Queensland Rail RMC will request a slot from the Downer Yardmaster
before routes into the Maintenance Facility can be set.
The Train Wash will also be accessible from the Mainline. Single train movements between the
Mainline and the Train Wash at the Northern End will not impact adversely on mainline operations.
Movement to/through the Train Wash and subsequently into Stabling will be controlled by
Queensland Rail RMC.
Movements between Mainline and Ormeau Facility are grouped as per the following:
 Mainline to the Ormeau Facility via the North – Figure 6:
 Mainline to the Ormeau Facility via the South – Figure 7:

5 Movements in the Maintenance
Facility
The available shunt necks on the north and south sides of the Maintenance Facility will create two
possible directions in which marshalling can occur within the Maintenance Facility. Examples of
south shunt neck moves would be a move from the Maintenance Facility to the Presentation Road
via the south neck or handing back a train from the Bio/Graffiti Wash to the Stabling Yard via the
south neck.
The movements can be grouped as per the following:
 Handover Location to Maintenance facility or special equipment
 Maintenance Facility or special equipment to Handback location.

and involves:

 The Maintenance Facility or special equipment road to a different Maintenance Facility
Road via the South Shunt neck.

6 Movements between the
Maintenance Facility and
Stabling
Movements between the Maintenance Facility and Ormeau Stabling Yard will be able to be
completed via either the north or south direction. Each of these movements will require an interface
and co-ordination between Queensland Rail RMC and the Downer Yardmaster to communicate
and plan the most effective time and direction of movement to meet Queensland Rail network
requirements and ensure no impact to network operations.
The movement interface agreement will need to consider run in and run out of Multiple Units. This
will require Handover locations and available Stabling positions to determine the time and direction
in which the movements will take place.
The movements via the north can be grouped as per the following:
 Figure 12 – Handover Location to Stabling Yard via the north
 Figure 13 – Stabling to Handover location via the north

Appendix 2 - Concept of
Operations – Maintenance
Facility
1 Maintenance Facility Capability
The Ormeau Maintenance Facility is designed to drive a step-change in fleet performance for the
QTMP Multiple Units. The Maintenance Facility comprises 4 roads in the maintenance facility, a
wheel lathe with bogie drop facility, a 2-road presentation platform, a graffiti removal and bio wash
building and a bypass road which includes a test track for maintaining the ETCS equipment on the
QTMP Multiple Units. The AVIS (Automatic Vehicle Inspection System) building is located on the
Train Wash road.
The Maintenance Facility is capable of servicing 80 QTMP Multiple Units on a 120-day
maintenance cycle
The Maintenance Facility is designed to provide the infrastructure necessary to deliver efficient
Whole of Life (WOL) maintenance activities to the QTMP fleet. It incorporates primary functions for
key work locations and is flexible in design to offer secondary functions for multiple locations.
The Maintenance Facility detail includes innovation, with one example being a sunken
design with a swimming pool to provide better access beneath the trains. It also supports
standard maintenance activities and Industry 4.0 capability, and the journey to predictive
maintenance through its Information and Communications Technology (ICT) capabilities
and integration of specialised equipment to the Asset Information System (AIS).
Table 13 highlights the key features and capabilities of the Maintenance Facility and Maintenance
Facility site.
Table 13: Maintenance Facility and Maintenance Facility Site Key Features, Functionality and Capability
Key Feature Key Functionally and Capability

 Pantograph Visual Inspection System

1.1 QTMP Maintenance Requirements
The planned preventative maintenance regime and forecasted corrective maintenance activities
have influenced the layout and design of the Ormeau Maintenance Facility. The frequency of
planned maintenance and the structure of the maintenance routine has further influenced the
number of roads required. The planned maintenance duration has been optimised to reduce any
impact to availability throughout the Multiple unit’s lifecycle. The operational preventative
maintenance exam (60 days) is to be undertaken overnight when the train is out of service thus
avoiding availability issues. The preventative balanced exams (120 days) will be completed during
the dayshift. Table 14 identifies key Multiple Unit Maintenance activities, their frequency and the
proposed location within the Maintenance Facility which is best equipped to complete the activity
safely and efficiently.
Table 14: Multiple Unit Maintenance requirements
Maintenance Description Interval Location

completed a detailed analysis on predicted corrective maintenance requirements to understand

any impact on the Ormeau Maintenance Facility’s capacity for unscheduled maintenance activities.
Our in-depth analysis has predicted how many times a Multiple Unit will return to the Maintenance
Facility, and what infrastructure and access will be required to efficiently repair and return the
Multiple Units to service without impacting existing planned maintenance activities within the
Maintenance Facility.
Figure 17 depicts a cross section of the Maintenance Facility building.
Figure 17: Ormeau Maintenance Facility section showing pit depths and platform locations
A detailed analysis of the QTMP Multiple Unit Overhaul and Midlife requirements has been
completed to understand the required space and infrastructure to effectively complete these
activities on-site at the Ormeau Maintenance Facility. The intention is to minimise any impact on
the continuing preventive and corrective maintenance activities that will occur within the
Maintenance Facility.
Each subsystem and its resources, parts, and infrastructure requirements have been mapped over
the QTMP Multiple unit lifecycle and predicted durations have been applied to each activity. This
analysis will inform the design and ensure that these activities can be completed effectively and in
parallel to ongoing maintenance. The approach ensures that the Maintenance Facility design can
support and enable all maintenance activity requirements without impacting on the availability of
Multiple Units.
1.3 Maintenance Facility Road Capability
Each maintenance road within the Maintenance Facility has been specifically designed to
create a primary capability to ensure QTMP Multiple Unit maintenance activities can be
performed effectively, whilst also incorporating design elements to provide secondary
capabilities.
This approach provides flexibility in design to support any unscheduled or unforeseen
impacts to maintenance activities. For example, Road 1 is a dedicated lift road primarily
designed to support the Multiple Unit Bogie overhaul programs and is designed on a raised
rail with pit and side access. This allows completion of corrective maintenance activities
when Bogie overhaul programs are not being completed.
Table 15 identifies each Maintenance Road and its primary and secondary capabilities.

2 Maintenance Facility - ‘Day in
the Life’
The Ormeau Maintenance Facility will be a 24/7 operation to support operational requirements and
allow multiple units to be handed over and handed back at any time. The shift patterns and
planned times for activities is modelled on an understanding of access to multiple units through
coordination with the Operator, and ad hoc opportunities when multiple units are stabled at the
Ormeau Stabling Yard.
Planned maintenance requirements will be communicated to the Operator to allow for operational
movements to work the units back to the Ormeau Maintenance Facility when preventive
maintenance activities are scheduled to occur. This will be the same process for any planned
corrective maintenance requirements.
Any unscheduled maintenance activities will be co-ordinated ad hoc via the Operator and the
IOC/Help desk to plan where the multiple units will be handed over when returned to the
Maintenance Facility.
Figure 18 depicts a typical ‘day in the life’ of the Ormeau Maintenance Facility over 24-hour
timeline and shows Multiple Units located at the Maintenance Facility to depict the maintenance
activities occurring on each set. It also shows the movements between the Maintenance Roads for
maintenance activities.
Within the context of the module, it has been assumed the sets have moved from, or will be moved
to, appropriate Handover and Handback locations before and after maintenance activities are
completed.
Figure 18: Ormeau Maintenance Facility over 24-hour Timeline Including Multiple Units
Downer EDI Limited
ABN 97 003 872 848 www.downergroup.com

Figure 19 demonstrates a typical day in the life of Ormeau Stabling and shows the expected sets
on site within a 24-hour period, including any expected durations of planned and unplanned
maintenance tasks.
Figure 19: Ormeau Stabling over 24-hour Timeline Including Multiple Units
2.1 Maintenance Facility Staff Structure
The Ormeau Maintenance Facility is to be staffed 24 hours a day, 7 days per week, so QTMP
Multiple Units can be attended to at any time. Maintenance Technicians will be available during
the day to undertake preventative maintenance, overhauls or corrective maintenance. The night
team of Technicians will be available to perform preventative or corrective maintenance.
Detailed cleans will be performed by cleaning staff overnight on the presentation platform. Daily
cleans will be carried out overnight in the Maintenance Facility and in the stabling yards throughout
the network.
3 Maintenance Facility
Stores/Office/Amenities
Adjacent to road 1 in the Maintenance facility will be offices, amenities, stores, and heavy
workshops. Administration, engineering, and maintenance management staff will work out of the
dedicated Office Area. This area will be used to control all activities at the Ormeau Maintenance
Facility. This convenient location will also be the site for shift pre-start briefings and daily work
allocations.
Downer EDI Limited
ABN 97 003 872 848 www.downergroup.com

[TABLE 1 on page 43]


--- PAGE 44 ---
QTMP-MNT-DOW-SM-RPT-000012 rev D
The Integrated Operation Centre (IOC) will be the eyes and ears of our operation. The IOC
operators will have access to online data streamed from the QTMP Multiple Units as well as
access to the Asset Information System (AIS) and location/train status from Fleet Network Display
(FND). The IOC will manage the fleet while in service and provide support to the RMC Help Desk.
The Maintenance Facility meal room will be a common area fitted out with cooking and
refrigeration equipment allowing staff to prepare meals and have a place away from their work area
to eat. Locker rooms will contain showers, toilets, and lockers for staff ablutions and a place to
secure personal belongings. The layout of the office and amenities is based around a central
corridor leading from the main entrance to the building. The briefing area is also adjacent to the
main corridor just prior to entering the train maintenance area.
The Maintenance Facility store is located between the electrical component workshop and bogie
workshop. There are two distinct stores areas, light man-handleable stores and heavy stores that
require a forklift. This is adjacent to the undercover delivery/dispatch area. The store has a
dedicated office located conveniently in this area.
The electrical component workshop is setup for repair of modules removed from the train as part of
repair or overhaul processes. In this workshop discrete components can be removed and replaced
and then tested prior to the module being returned to stock.
The bogie workshop is designed to handle overhaul of QTMP bogies. The setup will allow multiple
bogies to be stripped down simultaneously and for subcomponents to be removed and sent away
to specialist overhaulers. The frame, pipework and rubber components will be maintained on site.
3.1 Materials in stores
Below in Table 16 is a volume of heavy stores based on the rotables list for the base fleet. The
store area needs to hold these stores as a minimum. Additionally, there are several thousand
more small stores items and consumable items also needing to be in the stores area.
The stores area requires
 an area to hold received items prior to being booked in
 an area to hold items packed ready for dispatch
 a quarantine area for items not fit for use that require investigation
 a returns area for parts that have failed and require to be dispatched for repair
 a stores counter for issuing parts

3.2 Materials Handling in Heavy Stores
All deliveries will be received in the delivery area adjacent to the heavy stores area. Delivery trucks
will arrive and park under the covered delivery area. Dependant on the load to be unloaded and
the storage location, the overhead crane or forklift truck will be used.
The overhead crane unloading process will have a designated laydown area for loads removed
from the truck, to then allow transfer and pickup by the overhead crane that allows for loading into
the bogie shop area.
The forklift truck will have enough room to access loads that are positioned on either side or at any
position on the truck bed. These loads can then be delivered to the bogie shop or heavy stores
area.
Items will be delivered via Pallets or specialty stillage racks designed for the particular asset
(bogies HVACs etc) items in racks will be positioned in their designated storage area, items on
pallets can be transferred directly to their designated location on the fixed pallet racking in the
heavy stores area.

During the unloading and loading process, consideration needs to be made for cordoning off
pedestrian access and ensuring safe movements of cranes and forklifts.
When items are requested by staff via the stores counter, warehouse staff will utilise forklifts for
heavy items on pallets to deliver to the required location in the maintenance shed. They will utilise
the forklift access around the perimeter of the Maintenance Facility and via ramps to central
locations or deliver items to the apron of the appropriate maintenance road, to allow for use of the
maintenance road cranes to lift the item to the required location.
3.3 Materials Handling in Light Stores
Materials handling in light stores will operate as per the heavy stores with regard to unloading and
loading of deliveries, with the addition that some items may be delivered by couriers in small
vans/vehicles and in small boxes that that can be transferred by staff using manual handling
processes.
Item movement in the light stores will generally be completed by pallet truck or manual handling
processes. Items will be stored on shelving that can be reached by staff at ground level, and some
pallet racking that will be accessed by pallet truck.
When small items are requested that can be transferred via manual handling processes, items will
be exchanged via the stores counter between the warehouse and maintenance staff. All
transactions are required to be recorded in the AIS and the stores counter and warehouse area will
require Downer Corp WIFI and hard cable network access for multiple computers and mobile
devices.
Light stores will also house and control shared tooling and will require shadow boards, racking and
draws to hold torque wrenches, battery drills, and testing equipment.
3.4 Materials to lineside
Items for each preventive maintenance exam are predetermined and communicated to stores via
the AIS. These items are picked and placed on trolleys that are parked in a designate area in
stores ready for distribution than can be wheeled by hand when needed to the appropriate
maintenance road via the concrete pathways and maintenance road access ramps.
Specific corrective maintenance items that have been incorporated into the exam tasks will be
provided as per the descriptions in the light and heavy stores sections.
Specialist lineside cabinets will be positioned on the maintenance roads. These cabinets will
contain high use consumables aligned with the primary maintenance activities that will be
completed on each particular road. Via “milk run” process warehouse staff to maintain the contents
of each cabinet and ensure items are available when needed. These cabinets will also house
shared high usage tooling such as torque wrenches, battery powered drills and mutlimeters, which
are managed via mobile access to AIS via CORP wifi. Cabinets will require access to 240 power.
Each Technician will have a mobile tablet and tool bag. Lockers will be provided along the office
wall of the maintenance shed to store each Technicians tool bag and tablet.
Downer EDI Limited
ABN 97 003 872 848 www.downergroup.com
--- PAGE 48 ---
QTMP-MNT-DOW-SM-RPT-000012 rev D
4 Cleaner access
4.1 Maintenance Facility
Cleaning will predominately be completed on the presentation platform external to the Maintenance
Facility building. This is where daily and monthly mandated cleans will take place. The cleaning
teams will arrive at site and can begin their shift in the designated cleaner’s space adjacent to the
meals room. From here they will move to the Presentation Platform where storage lockers located
at the platform will house all the required chemicals, consumables and equipment needed to
complete presentation activities. Safe and efficient pedestrian access should be provided for all
locations where presentation activities will occur.
As required these lockers/cabinet will need access to 240V power to charge any powered
equipment and water will be accessible on the platform. Trains will be parked and isolated from
movement and power (when required) via the DPPS system to allow cleaners to complete
activities safety.
Normal detailed cleaning will be conducted with OHLE on and train powered up. In the event of a
manual exterior clean the OHLE will need to be isolated as cleaners will be using jet washes.
Cleaners will access the trains via the platform and train doors and move through the train from
one end to another completing the required activities. Visual aids will be placed in the crew cabs on
each end to inform staff that presentation staff are present on the set.
When complete, cleaners will pack up and return all equipment to the lockers and make their way
via pedestrian access back to their lunch/meeting room.
When required cleaners will clean the nosecone ends on the train sets by accessing a retractable
drawbridge platform which is interlocked with the DPPS and at track level and using equipment to
reach and scrub the front of the sets.
Also, as required, spot cleaning may be required on sets within the Maintenance Facility building.
Under the control of the Maintenance Delivery Manager cleaners will be granted access to sets to
perform required spot cleaning. They will carry the requirement equipment with them to perform
activities, returning to the presentation platform when complete. They will access the sets via
pedestrian access and fixed stairways/platforms in the Maintenance Facility.
Some bulk storage of cleaning consumables may also be stored in the light stores. Cleaners will
access the stores counter as required via pedestrian pathways to access additional consumables
to replenish storage cabinets located at the presentation platform.
4.2 Stabling Yard
A specific cleaner’s space is part of the Rail Traffic Crew building for set cleaners to meet, store
equipment and materials, and have breaktime. The location in the Rail Traffic Crew building will
require 240V power to charge various pieces of cleaning equipment and also require a wet and dry
stores for cleaning chemicals and cleaning materials.
Co ordinating with the stabling yard controller, cleaning staff will access sets stabled in the yard to
perform presentation activities. They will carry the required equipment from the designated area in
the Rail Traffic Crew building to the sets requiring cleaning. They will access the set via pedestrian
pathways and fixed platforms to access each set crew cab door and move through the set
performing presentation activities. Visual aids will be placed in the crew cabs on each end to inform
staff that presentation staff are present on the set.
Downer EDI Limited
ABN 97 003 872 848 www.downergroup.com
--- PAGE 49 ---
QTMP-MNT-DOW-SM-RPT-000012 rev D
The Technicians from the Maintenance Facility will access the trains via a pathway from the
Maintenance Facility using an electronic controlled access system through a controlled access
gate.
Technician activities include driving the sanding cart from the sand silo by the Maintenance Facility
building to the trains to top up the sand on an unobstructed continuous path. The Technicians will
also be required to test the sanding systems and clean up the ejected sand. The sand cart is
required to be stored in a secure and weatherproof area.
Access at ground level will be required to top up the screen wash in each cab. This is located
below the driving cab at each end.
Access at ground level will be required at vehicle 3 and 4 to top up the fresh water tank.
Access at ground level will be required at vehicle 3 and 4 to decant the waste water tank, rinse the
tank and decant the rinse water.
5 Graffiti Cleaning and BIO wash
As required, specialised presentation staff will use the specialist graffiti cleaning and bio wash
facility to perform graffiti removal and bio cleaning after animal and human strikes. Train sets will
be positioned and isolated from movement and power in the appropriate location to access the
area of the set requiring cleaning.
In the Graffiti area access to the lower side, passenger door level, and topside of the set will be
needed to reach all car side panel areas of the train to allow cleaning. A combination of fixed
platform and mobile platforms on both sides of the set will allow cleaners to position, access and
clean all areas of the set. If the graffiti is longer than one car length, the train set will need to be
repositioned as required to allow access to clean.
Cleaners will access the specialist cleaning area via pedestrian access pathways, and storage
cabinets and lockers will be required to sore equipment and cleaning consumables in the graffiti
cleaning building.
6 Maintenance activities outside
the Maintenance Facility
building
As required, the maintenance activities on the Multiple Units outside the Train Maintenance Facility
building (TMF) may include provisioning using the mobile decanting vehicle. The emptying of the
mobile decanting vehicle will be conducted at dedicated connections on the north and south of the
TMF in the handover/handback locations.
Sandbox replenishment may be conducted in the areas north and south of the TMF using the
mobile sand carts.
Preventative and corrective maintenance activities may also be conducted on Multiple Units
ensuring the tasks have been risk assessed and suitable controls applied in accordance with TLS
safety management system.
Pathways/walkways and lighting shall be designed to MD-12-708 standard.
Downer EDI Limited
ABN 97 003 872 848 www.downergroup.com
--- PAGE 50 ---
QTMP-MNT-DOW-SM-RPT-000012 rev D
7 Maintenance activities inside
TMF
7.1 Windscreen Removal
Access to the windscreen at train floor level will be required to remove the windscreen. The
location for this activity will be on roads 2-4 as there is a need for an overhead crane so the
windscreen can be lifted out.
7.2 Train lift and bogie removal
The train will be positioned on the train lift so that all the bogies are on the lift. The Technicians will
disconnect the bogies to be removed. The train will be lifted up. The anvils will be inserted in
under the body at the lifting points to support the body and the lift will be lowered. As the bogies
are already disconnected from the body, those bogies due for removal will be lowered back on to
the track. A battery electric tug will be used to push the bogies out from under the train. As each
bogie reaches the bogie turn table it will be turned and then pushed to the bogie workshop.
The refit process is the reverse of the removal process start from the bogie workshop.
7.3 DPPS / OHW isolation
Each road where a maintenance activity can be performed should be protected by a DPPS system
and OHW isolation should be available and interlocked with the DPPS if there is a danger of
contact with the OHW during maintenance activities.
DPPS should:
 protect the maintenance workers from vehicle movements whilst maintenance workers are
tagged on and undertaking work on the train
 prevent equipment being left fowling the protected road when protection is removed
 protect the maintenance workers from accessing roof platforms when no train is present
 protect the maintenance workers from coming into contact with live OHW
 protect the maintenance workers when using jet wash equipment on presentation road
7.4 Rollingstock equipment removal, details,
dimensions
Table 17, Table 18, and Table 19 describe details to be considered in the design of the facilities.

7.5 Swimming Pool Forklift
Assume Forklift approaches equipment along the L (length) side of the item.
Forklift spec example 3 tonne with 2m forks -

The graffiti removal facility is designed to accommodate a single carriage at a time. This is on the
assumption that the graffiti to be removed is discrete and covers a relatively short length of the
train. Any graffiti that is applied along the whole train (like a spray applied as the train drives past
the vandal), will require the train to be moved through the graffiti removal facility to complete the
full removal.

9 Durations of Movements within
the Ormeau Facility
To demonstrate how the Ormeau Facility may be operated, a high-level model has been developed
of possible movements that may occur within the Facility. An assessment was made of the run
time to go from one point to another within the facility to verify that the proposed design is
consistent with the expected cycles of the rollingstock maintenance processes. Findings provide
additional evidence that the proposed layout is appropriate from an operational viewpoint.
9.1 Mapping of activities and movements within the
Ormeau Facility
As part of the verification process, Downer’s Through Life Support Team created a list of activities
and movements that may occur within the Ormeau Facility during a high period of utilisation. These
activities and movements were mapped and calculated to highlight operational issues or
shortcomings in the assumptions.
Figure 20 demonstrates the high-level initial assessment of the activities, movements, and track
utilisation within the Ormeau Facility.

9.2 Assumptions
Assumptions about activities and movements:
 A blanket travel speed for trains moving through the Maintenance Facility of 8kph, with
allowance for acceleration and deceleration.
 A travel speed for trains moving through the Train Wash of 3kph
 A walking speed through the Facility of 4kph
 One Rail Traffic Crew is available at the Facility for shunting moves in addition to the
Queensland Rail mainline Rail Traffic Crews that operate the trains in and out of the Facility.
This may be a full-time Rail Traffic Crew or shared between Rail Traffic Crews that also drive
the mainline trains
 One Downer crew is available at the Facility
 A handover time between Rail Traffic Crew and Downer crews of 10 minutes to conduct train
condition assessments where trains are coming from revenue service to the Maintenance
Facility for maintenance
 Departure movements for the AM period are omitted as they do not clash with these planned
movements.

9.3 Details of typical movements and actions within
the Ormeau Facility
To illustrate the solution, Table 22 lists the details of the typical movements and actions that occur
within the Ormeau Facility, including estimated speed, distance, and time. These follow a basic
calculation to derive the amount of time taken for each movement or action to occur, including an
allowance for acceleration and deceleration, where appropriate.
Additionally, static assumptions have been made regarding the amount of time required for the
Handover between crews to occur and the amount of time required for a turnback action to take
place. These timings have been applied to form a more comprehensive schedule in Appendix 3
.

QTMP-MNT-DOW-SM-RPT-000012 rev B
Appendix 3 is an output of the Excel modelling of a 24-hour day within the Maintenance Facility
and Stabling train and crew movements. It captures the sequence of train and crew movements
presented for a high-utilisation operating day. This demonstrates that the operations can be
achieved with a single Downer crew and a single Rail Traffic Crew.
For each set moving between the Maintenance Facility, Stabling Yard, and mainline; there are
three rows to represent the utilisation of:
 Downer crew
 Rail Traffic Crew located at the Facility.
 Rail Traffic Crew entering or exiting the Facility from the mainline.
Sets that run exclusively between mainline and Stabling Yard only have one row that shows the
utilisation and timing of their arrival/departure from the Facility.
The Rail Traffic Crewlocated within the Stabling Yard will experience a comparatively low utilisation
compared with the Downer crew. This is due to the low number of moves between the Stabling
Yard and Maintenance Facility, with most trains entering and exiting the Facility from the mainline.
The results demonstrate that even on a day where the Maintenance Facility utilisation is higher
than planned, there is sufficient time to move the Multiple Units around to complete the required
maintenance and return them to Stabling for re-entry into service. The utilisation of the dedicated
Queensland Rail Maintenance Facility Rail Traffic Crew achieves a lower result, which is likely not
required. We note that the duties of the Queensland Rail Maintenance Facility Rail Traffic Crew
could be achieved using crews from mainline trains.
The Excel model depicted in Appendix 3 shows one minute time increments and the cells are
colour coded as per Table 24.
Table 24: Appendix 3 colour coding guide
Task or utilisation Colour code
Trains arriving from the mainline, including a Dark green, bright green float
minimum two-minute float
Additional allowance/recovery/idle time between Pale green
tasks
Handover between Queensland Rail and Downer Orange
Crew walking Blue
Train movements within the Facility Brown
Downer Maintenance Facility crew utilisation Purple
Queensland Rail Stabling Rail Traffic Crew utilisation Pink
The train movements within the Ormeau Facility are modelled using a representation of a day’s
operation that is more congested than the expected operation. The modelling shows that a single
Downer train crew and utilisation of Rail Traffic Crews can achieve the necessary train movements
to accomplish all maintenance activities.
Ultimately, trains can be returned to the Stabling Yard prior to entry into service, which allows
trains entering service to achieve the mainline headway requirements.
